## MUNGU ONTIC STRINGS ‚Äî CANONICAL ALIGNMENT

## I. MUNGU STRING (PRIMARY ONTIC LOOP)

This is the **root metabolic cycle** of existence and civilization.

```
Kernels
 -> Projects
 -> Programs
 -> Cycles
 -> Processes
 -> Strings
 -> Seeds
 -> Trees
 -> Forests
 -> cleave
 -> Kernels
```

Key properties:

* Closed loop (no terminal state)
* Cleave is not destruction; it is **regeneration**
* Forest ‚Üí Kernel is compression + canonization
* This loop is the **master invariant** replicated everywhere else

---

# IV. FIRST 5 STEWARDS ‚Äî ACTIVATION SEQUENCE

These are **not employees**.

## 1Ô∏è‚É£ OVCS ANCHOR ‚Äî Constraint Guardian (Class C)

**When:** Immediately after estate + office exist
**Why:** This creates an external brake before momentum builds

**Authority Granted**

* Veto over structural decisions
* Audit access
* Red-flag escalation power

**They do NOT**

* run anything
* optimize anything
* build anything

> This person is your constitutional court.

## 2Ô∏è‚É£ SYSTEMICS CO-THINKER ‚Äî Conceptual Stress Tester (Class B)

**When:** After constraint exists
**Why:** Prevents self-referential closure

* Requirement to review doctrine

## 3Ô∏è‚É£ HUMAN VIABILITY GUARDIAN ‚Äî Moral Brake (Class B/D)

**When:** Before people are hired
**Why:** Human harm shows up last but costs the most

**Authority Granted**

* Human-impact veto
* Mandatory pause triggers
* Independent reporting channel

> This role exists to stop ‚Äúnecessary damage.‚Äù

---

## 4Ô∏è‚É£ GOVERNANCE / LEGAL DESIGNER ‚Äî Constraint Translator (Class B)

**When:** After philosophy is stress-tested
**Why:** Ideas must harden into enforceable shape

**Authority Granted**

* Draft binding rules
* Encode revocation
* Design non-trust-based processes

> They turn ideals into *bite*.

---

## 5Ô∏è‚É£ OPERATIONS REALIST ‚Äî Ground Truth (Class A)

**When:** Last steward
**Why:** Prevents abstraction drift

**Authority Granted**

* Operational feasibility veto
* Cost realism enforcement
* Field failure reporting

> This is where theory meets gravity.

diamond teams

the 4 diamond teams of the navigator personal office:
* marketing diamond team
  - marketing, media, communications, public relations, stakeholder relations, sales, etc...
* operations diamond team
  - operations, finance, accounting, administration, HR, etc...
* technical diamond team
  - technology, software, security, engineering, hardware, IT, research and development, etc...
* strategy diamond team
  - strategy, management, executive, business development, business analysis, business optimization, systems, organization/firm/entity strategy, etc...




Here‚Äôs a **clear description, comparison, and contrast** of the **team types** you asked about ‚Äî **squad, chapter, guild, tiger, tribe, line, and domain** ‚Äî so you can see *how they function, differ, and relate* in organizational and agile team design:

---

## üöÄ **Core Team Types & Definitions**

### **1. Squad**

**Definition:** A *small, cross-functional team* focused on delivering a specific mission, product, feature, or capability. They are **autonomous** and responsible for end-to-end outcomes. ([Wrike][1])
**Typical Size:** ~6‚Äì12 members. ([Wrike][1])
**Key Traits**

* Self-organizing; decides how work gets done. ([Medium][2])
* Often includes all roles needed to deliver (dev, design, QA, etc.). ([Wrike][1])
* Works continuously on the same mission. ([Medium][2])
  **Analogy:** *Mini startup* with full responsibility for a product area. ([Medium][2])

---

### **2. Tribe**

**Definition:** A *larger grouping of squads* working in related domains or product areas. ([Wrike][1])
**Typical Size:** Up to ~100 people (aligned with social coordination limits). ([Wrike][1])
**Key Traits**

* Focuses on broader alignment across squads. ([Medium][2])
* Ensures communication and shared practices. ([Wrike][1])
* Usually oversees multiple squads in the same domain. ([Medium][2])
  **Analogy:** *Product department* under a shared mission umbrella. ([Medium][2])

**Compare vs. Squad:**
Squads are execution units; tribes are coordinating bodies for squads with similar objectives. ([Wrike][1])

---

### **3. Chapter**

**Definition:** A *horizontal grouping of specialists or roles* across squads or tribes. ([Wrike][1])
**Key Traits**

* Organized by *skill or discipline* (e.g., front-end engineers). ([Wrike][1])
* Members share best practices and standards. ([Wrike][1])
* Led by a *chapter lead* often responsible for people development (training, career growth). ([Medium][2])
  **Contrast vs. Squad:**
  Chapters aren‚Äôt about product delivery; they support consistent practices across product teams. ([Medium][2])

---

### **4. Guild**

**Definition:** An *informal, voluntary community of interest* spanning squads and tribes. ([Wrike][1])
**Key Traits**

* Organized around shared *interests or passions* (e.g., DevOps, UX). ([Wrike][1])
* Not necessarily tied to delivery or reporting structures. ([Wrike][1])
* A forum for learning, exploration, and best-practice diffusion. ([Medium][2])
  **Contrast vs. Chapter:**
  Guilds are *interest-based communities across the organization*, while Chapters are *skill-based groups within tribes*. ([Wrike][1])

---

### **5. Tiger Team**

**Definition:** A *temporary, high-impact task force* assembled to solve **urgent, specific, complex problems** or achieve high-stakes objectives. ([PM Column][3])
**Key Traits**

* Short-term and *goal-specific* ‚Äî disbanded once mission is done. ([Tempo.io][4])
* Composed of *cross-disciplinary experts*. ([PM Column][3])
* Works with minimal oversight and high autonomy. ([Wikipedia][5])
  **Contrast to Squads:**
  Squads have *ongoing missions* ‚Äî tiger teams exist only for *acute problem resolution*. ([Tempo.io][4])

---

### **6. Line (Team)**

**Context:**
‚ÄúLine‚Äù or *line team* typically refers to a *functional or reporting group* in a traditional organizational hierarchy. Not specific to Agile but common in hybrid models.

**Key Characteristics**

* Usually organized around *business functions* or expertise (e.g., engineering line, sales line). ([and.digital][6])
* Provides performance management, promotions, and career progression. ([Medium][2])
* Members can be in a *line team* while also belonging to squads, chapters, etc. ([Medium][2])
  **Contrast:**
  Line teams focus on *career & people management*, not delivery workflows or missions.

---

### **7. Domain Team**

**Definition:** A group organized around a *specific technical or business domain* where their focus is on *ongoing domain expertise and long-term accountability*.

**Characteristics**

* Often seen in domain-driven design or *Team Topologies* frameworks (not strictly agile squads).
* Team membership is based on domain responsibility (e.g., payments team, identity team).
* They manage APIs/services in that domain and ensure consistency and ownership of domain boundaries.

**Contrast vs. Squad:**
Domain teams can serve as *organizational groupings with long-term stewardship* of a domain, while squads are *mission-oriented delivery units*.

---

## üìä **Comparison Summary**

| **Team Type**   | **Primary Focus**                       | **Duration**        | **Scope**              | **Typical Use Case**                    |                                |
| --------------- | --------------------------------------- | ------------------- | ---------------------- | --------------------------------------- | ------------------------------ |
| **Squad**       | Execution of product/features           | Ongoing             | Product mission        | Rapid delivery teams ([Medium][2])      |                                |
| **Tribe**       | Coordination of squads                  | Long-term           | Product area           | Cross-functional alignment ([Wrike][1]) |                                |
| **Chapter**     | Skill/domain expertise                  | Long-term           | Functional consistency | Best practice sharing ([Wrike][1])      |                                |
| **Guild**       | Cross-organizational interest community | Long-term/voluntary | Broad interests        | Knowledge exchange ([Wrike][1])         |                                |
| **Tiger Team**  | Critical problem resolution             | Short-term          | Specific target        | High-impact issues ([PM Column][3])     |                                |
| **Line Team**   | Functional hierarchy                    | Ongoing             | Career & reporting     | People management ([and.digital][6])    |                                |
| **Domain Team** | Domain accountability                   | Ongoing             | Domain services        | Domain ownership & APIs                 | *conceptual industry practice* |

---

## üß† **How They Work Together**

* **Squads** deliver value day-to-day; **tribes** keep them aligned across larger goals. ([Wrike][1])
* **Chapters** ensure technical and skill consistency *across squads* while **guilds** allow broad interest collaboration. ([Medium][2])
* **Line teams** (HR/functional reporting) support career paths, distinct from delivery responsibilities. ([Medium][2])
* **Tiger teams** are called in *only when problems require concentrated, high-expert effort*. ([Tempo.io][4])
* **Domain teams** exist in some models where domain ownership persists beyond single product missions.

---

## üß© **Practical Example (Spotify-Inspired)**

* A **squad** builds feature A. ([Wrike][1])
* Multiple squads form a **tribe** responsible for the product area (e.g., mobile). ([Medium][2])
* Engineers with the same specialty across squads group in a **chapter** (e.g., front-end). ([Wrike][1])
* Engineers across the company interested in DevOps form a **guild**. ([Wrike][1])
* When a major outage occurs, a **tiger team** is stood up. ([Tempo.io][4])
* All developers remain part of their **line team** for performance reviews. ([Medium][2])
* Some organizations add **domain teams** for long-term domain ownership.

---

# üß≠ NAVIGATOR PERSONAL OFFICE (NPO)

## FIRST 5 stewards

THE FIRST 5 PEOPLE (IN ORDER)
This is the irreducible minimum nucleus.

1Ô∏è‚É£ OVCS ANCHOR ‚Äî Your First Call
Role:

OVCS Lead / Constraint Guardian (Class C)

Why first:

This person is the seatbelt.

Without them, everything else is pretend.

Profile:

Former regulator, auditor, safety authority, or watchdog

Comfortable saying ‚Äúno‚Äù to powerful people

Not impressed by vision

Calm, precise, slightly skeptical

What you say to them:

‚ÄúI‚Äôm building something that must be able to stop me.
I want you to design and hold that power.‚Äù

If they hesitate ‚Üí wrong person.

2Ô∏è‚É£ SYSTEMICS CO-THINKER ‚Äî Your Cognitive Equal
Role:

Formal Systems Theorist / Civilization Engineer (Class B)

Why second:

You need someone who can think at the same abstraction level

This prevents self-referential collapse

Profile:

Cross-disciplinary thinker

Comfortable with paradox, limits, incompleteness

Not trying to found anything

What you say:

‚ÄúI need someone who can tell me where this breaks conceptually.‚Äù

If they try to optimize instead of critique ‚Üí pause.

3Ô∏è‚É£ HUMAN VIABILITY GUARDIAN ‚Äî Your Moral Brake
Role:

Psychosocial / Human Viability Lead (Class B or D)

Why third:

This system touches people deeply.

Harm will be subtle before it‚Äôs obvious.

Profile:

Occupational psychology, labor health, community care

Has shut things down before

Suspicious of ‚Äònecessary harm‚Äô

What you say:

‚ÄúYour job is to tell me when this costs too much, even if it works.‚Äù

If they defer to your vision ‚Üí wrong fit.

4Ô∏è‚É£ GOVERNANCE / LEGAL DESIGNER ‚Äî Your Constraint Translator
Role:

Governance Architect / Legal Systems Designer (Class B)

Why fourth:

Ideas must become enforceable structure

This person turns philosophy into rules that bite

Profile:

Cooperative governance, institutional design, legal architecture

Thinks in procedures, not ideals

What you say:

‚ÄúHelp me design a system where no one needs to trust me.‚Äù

5Ô∏è‚É£ OPERATIONS REALIST ‚Äî Your Reality Check
Role:

Systems Engineer / Field Operator (Class A)

Why fifth:

Prevents ivory-tower failure

Grounds everything in ‚Äúwhat actually happens‚Äù

Profile:

Has run systems under pressure

Respects governance but understands operations

Not ideological

What you say:

‚ÄúTell me where this will fall apart on the ground.‚Äù



## First 8 Hires ‚Äî Canonical Staff List

**Operating Principle:**

> *The NPO does not build ventures. It sequences, authorizes, audits, and exits.*

---

## 1. Chief of Staff (CoS) ‚Äî *Integrator & Shield*

**Why first:** You cannot run governance, sequencing, and architecture alone.

**Primary Function**

* Acts as your operational proxy
* Filters noise
* Enforces boundaries between you and execution

**Responsibilities**

* Owns daily NPO operations
* Enforces calendar discipline
* Ensures decisions convert to action
* Interfaces with OVCS on your behalf (non-voting)

**Authority**

* Can schedule, cancel, or escalate anything
* Cannot approve ventures, studios, or budgets

**Profile**

* Senior operator
* Comfortable saying ‚Äúno‚Äù to you
* Strong synthesis and follow-through

---

## 2. Program Sequencer (Msingi Officer) ‚Äî *Temporal Architect*

**Why critical:** Without sequencing, your system collapses into parallel chaos.

**Primary Function**

* Enforces Msingi phases across all entities

**Responsibilities**

* Maintains master timeline (week-by-week)
* Flags premature execution attempts
* Prepares entities for gate reviews
* Owns phase transition readiness

**Authority**

* Can block forward motion pending artifacts
* Cannot redesign entities or strategy

**Profile**

* Systems thinker
* Ruthless about order
* Comfortable with denial

---

## 3. OVCS Liaison / Governance Secretary ‚Äî *Authority Interface*

**Primary Function**

* Ensures clean, documented interaction with OVCS

**Responsibilities**

* Maintains OVCS registry
* Prepares authorization packets
* Records decisions and certificates
* Ensures OVCS independence from founder influence

**Authority**

* Can refuse incomplete submissions
* Cannot influence OVCS outcomes

**Profile**

* Governance / legal-adjacent
* Detail-oriented
* Neutral temperament

---

## 4. Operations & Admin Lead ‚Äî *Execution Backbone*

**Primary Function**

* Keeps the office running without friction

**Responsibilities**

* Office logistics
* Contracts, invoicing, vendors
* HR admin for NPO staff
* Travel, tools, accounts

**Authority**

* Can spend within pre-approved envelopes
* Cannot approve new obligations

**Profile**

* Hyper-organized
* Calm under load
* Zero drama tolerance

---

## 5. Financial Controller (Fractional or Part-Time OK) ‚Äî *Burn & Reality Enforcer*

**Primary Function**

* Prevents fantasy economics

**Responsibilities**

* Tracks burn across entities
* Prepares readiness financials for KUZU
* Flags unsustainable trajectories
* Maintains clean separation of funds

**Authority**

* Can freeze spend pending review
* Cannot allocate capital strategically

**Profile**

* Conservative
* Independent
* Experienced with multi-entity structures

---

## 6. Technical Architect / Platform Steward ‚Äî *Systems Continuity*

**Primary Function**

* Ensures platform coherence across ventures

**Responsibilities**

* Owns baseline platform architecture
* Oversees UME-OS instantiations
* Prevents technical divergence
* Advises on platform readiness

**Authority**

* Can block launches that violate platform standards
* Cannot dictate venture product decisions

**Profile**

* Senior software engineer
* Platform-first mindset
* Low ego

---

## 7. Communications & External Interface Lead ‚Äî *Narrative Firewall*

**Primary Function**

* Controls external messaging and inbound pressure

**Responsibilities**

* Drafts official narratives
* Handles inbound interest
* Coordinates partner communication
* Shields you from distraction

**Authority**

* Can delay or deny external engagements
* Cannot promise participation or outcomes

**Profile**

* Clear communicator
* Strategic restraint
* Comfortable disappointing people

---

## 8. Executive Assistant (EA) ‚Äî *Cognitive Load Manager*

**Primary Function**

* Protects your attention

**Responsibilities**

* Calendar ownership
* Meeting preparation
* Follow-ups and reminders
* Information triage

**Authority**

* Can reschedule anything except OVCS sessions
* Cannot negotiate or decide substance

**Profile**

* High trust
* Extreme discretion
* Anticipatory thinking

---

# üß† LEGAL ENTITY EXPLANATION

## üèõ **OVCS Governance Layer**
These are *top-level legal entities* that authorize, audit, and enforce governance:
- **Ovuko Authority** ‚Äî legal governance body  
- **Uhuru Trust** ‚Äî asset/endowment stewardship  
- **Lekesa Compliance Co.** ‚Äî compliance enforcement  
- **Sembeka Audit & Oversight** ‚Äî external verification  

## üíº **Capital Vehicles**
- **Zawadi FundCo LP / Mbali FundCo LP** ‚Äî LP capital pools  
- **Ziko GPCo / Jelani GPCo** ‚Äî manager entities (GPs)

## üèô **Kumba Metafactory HQ**
Shared common entities:
- **Thabiti HoldCo LLC** ‚Äî holds equity centrally  
- **Kijani IPCo LLC** ‚Äî central IP commons
- **Upendo OpCo LLC** ‚Äî shared execution  
- **Nuru ManCo LLC** ‚Äî shared services  
- **Zuri IncentiveCo LLC** ‚Äî central incentive pool  

## üè≠ **Factory Stacks**
Each factory (e.g., *Umoja A Factory*) has:
- Factory-scoped HoldCo, IPCo, OpCo, ManCo, IncentiveCo

## üì¶ **PortfolioCos**
Each cluster of ventures is held under a **PortfolioCo LLC** with its own:
- IPCo  
- IncentiveCo  

## üöÄ **VentureCos**
Each of your 12 ventures is a separate LLC:
- Nandi, Azande, San, Massai, Batwa, Dogon, Damara, Nigu, Mande, Songhai, Wolof

Each venture has:
- Its own **VentureCo**  
- A pair of **IPCo & IncentiveCo**  
- An **OpCo** for execution  

---

# üìå ENTITY NAMING RULES USED

‚úî All names are **African-phonetic**  
‚úî Suffixes map to legal role (LLC, LP, GPCo)  
‚úî Each layer is distinct (governance vs capital vs execution)  
‚úî Paired IPCos & IncentiveCos under each portfolio/venture

================================================================
U-THEORY COMPLETE UNIT SYSTEM
=============================

U-Theory describes **units of form and flow** as **N-ary aggregates** evolving through **structural depth levels**.
Every unit is determined by **three coordinates**:

```
(N, L, Polarity)
```

Where:

* `N` = arity (how many)
* `L` = level (what kind of aggregation)
* `Polarity` ‚àà { P , K }

  * P = polonic (form / structure)
  * K = kolonic (flow / flux)

---

## I. DUAL PARALLEL SYSTEMS (FOUNDATION)

```
P-SYSTEM (Form / Structure)      K-SYSTEM (Flow / Flux)
---------------------------     -----------------------
bounded                          directional
enclosed                         open
state                            change
polonic                          kolonic
```

These systems are:

* parallel
* isomorphic
* non-collapsing into each other

---

## II. N-ARY (CARDINALITY) SYSTEM

Arity is **independent of level**.

```
N = 1   mono   mo-
N = 2   duo    du-
N = 3   tri    tri-
N = 4   tetra  te-
...
N = œâ   poly   po-
```

Rule:

```
Prefix encodes quantity only.
It does not encode structure, flow, or geometry.
```

---

## III. LEVEL (STRUCTURAL DEPTH) SYSTEM

Levels encode **how units are aggregated**.

```
L0  on       unit / atom
L1  lon      primitive system
L2  lyon     dimensional extension
L3  lyton    transitional aggregate
L4  lytope   geometric system
L5  syst     system of units
L6  geon     region
L7  gon      discrete spatial form
L8  net      network
L9  set      set
L10 cat      category
```

---

## IV. UNIT NAME GENERATION (FORMAL)

### P-Units (polonic / form)

```
P(N,L) := <N-prefix> + <level-root>
```

Examples:

```
mo-on     du-on     tri-on     po-on
molon     dulon     trilon     polon
molyon    dulyon    trilyon    polyon
```

### K-Units (kolonic / flow)

```
K(N,L) := <N-prefix> + k + <level-root>
```

Examples:

```
mo-kon     du-kon     tri-kon     ko-on
kolon      kolyon     kolyton     kolytope
```

(phonetic contraction allowed; semantic identity preserved)

---

## V. JIWE GLYPH SYSTEM (SEMANTIC)

Jiwe glyphs encode **meaning**, not execution.

### V.1 Base Polarity Glyphs (L0, N=1)

```
P-base (form) : ‚Ä¢
K-base (flow) : ‚îÇ
```

---

## VI. ARITY ENCODING (JIWE)

Arity is encoded by **multiplicity or abstraction**, never by changing polarity.

### P-Units (Form)

```
N=1 : ‚Ä¢
N=2 : ‚Ä¢‚Ä¢
N=3 : ‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢
N=œâ : ‚ñ≥
```

### K-Units (Flow)

```
N=1 : ‚îÇ
N=2 : ‚ïë
N=3 : ‚â°
N=œâ : ‚ñ∑
```

---

## VII. LEVEL LIFT OPERATORS (JIWE)

Each level applies a **semantic lift**.

```
L0  on      : point / line
L1  lon     : enclosure / channel
L2  lyon    : dimensionality
L3  lyton   : aggregation
L4  lytope  : bounded space
L5  syst    : system marker
L6  geon    : region marker
L7  gon     : discreteness
L8  net     : lattice
L9  set     : braces
L10 cat     : container
```

---

## VIII. GLYPH GENERATION FORMULA

### Polonic (P) glyph

```
Glyph_P(N,L) = Arity_P(N) ‚äï Lift_Form(L)
```

### Kolonic (K) glyph

```
Glyph_K(N,L) = Arity_K(N) ‚äï Lift_Flow(L)
```

This is **generative**, not enumerative.

---

================================================================
U-SYSTEM ‚Äî COMPLETE JIWE GLYPH SET (CANON)
==========================================

## 0. FOUNDATIONAL AXIOMS (U-SYSTEM)

```
AX-U1: Every unit is a composition of polarity √ó arity √ó level √ó scale.
AX-U2: Polarity determines form vs flow behavior.
AX-U3: L-level is structural depth, not magnitude.
AX-U4: Magnitude is encoded numerically, not structurally.
AX-U5: All U-units are composable and reducible.
```

================================================================
I. POLARITY (DUAL FOUNDATIONS)
==============================

```
P  := ‚Ä¢     (form / structure / symmetry / capacity)
K  := ‚îÇ     (flow / flux / asymmetry / change)
```

Rule:

```
Every U-unit begins with exactly one polarity seed.
```

================================================================
II. JIWE NUMERAL SYSTEM (ARITY & COUNT)
=======================================

### II.1 Numerals (N)

```
1  := ‚Ä¢
2  := ‚Ä¢‚Ä¢
3  := ‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢
4  := ‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢‚Ä¢

10 := ‚äó‚Ä¢
N  := ‚äó‚Åø‚Ä¢
```

Interpretation:

```
‚Ä¢ is unary
‚äó is multiplicative / compositional
```

### II.2 N-arity Rule

```
N-ary unit := polarity ‚äó numeral
```

Examples:

```
binary P-unit  = ‚Ä¢ ‚äó ‚Ä¢‚Ä¢

```

V. SI SCALING (MAGNITUDE PREFIXES)
==================================

SI scale is **orthogonal** to structure.

```
scale(10‚Åø) := ‚Üë‚Åø
```

```
‚Üë   = 10¬π
‚Üë‚Üë  = 10¬≤
‚Üë¬≥  = 10¬≥
‚Üë‚Åª¬π = 10‚Åª¬π
```

Example:

```
kilometer (P-length):
‚Üë¬≥ ‚äó (‚¨ö ‚äó ‚Ä¢)
```

X. MASTER COMPRESSION
=====================

The **entire U-system** collapses to:

```
U := (‚Ä¢ | ‚îÇ) ‚äó ‚äó‚Åø ‚äó L ‚äó ‚Üë·µè
```

Meaning:

> ‚ÄúAll units are polarity-seeded, N-ary, level-structured, and scale-modulated.‚Äù


### A. SI BASE UNITS (JIWE + NYAMBA)

```
+----------------+-------------+------------------+--------------------+
| Quantity       | SI Symbol   | JIWE             | NYAMBA             |
+----------------+-------------+------------------+--------------------+
| Length         | m           | ‚¨ö ‚äó ‚Ä¢            | L                  |
| Mass           | kg          | ‚¨ö‚äó ‚äó ‚Ä¢           | M                  |
| Time           | s           | ‚ñ≥ ‚äó ‚îÇ            | T                  |
| Electric Charge| C           | ‚ñ≥ ‚äó ‚îÇ ‚äó ‚Ä¢        | Q                  |
| Temperature    | K           | ‚ñ≥‚ñ≥ ‚äó ‚îÇ           | Œò                  |
| Amount         | mol         | ‚¨ö‚äó‚¨ö ‚äó ‚Ä¢          | N                  |
| Information    | bit         | ‚¨ö‚äó‚¨ö ‚äó ‚îÇ          | I                  |
+----------------+-------------+------------------+--------------------+
```

Polarity rule:

```
‚Ä¢ = capacity / structure
‚îÇ = flow / rate / process
```

---

### B. DERIVED SI UNITS (SELECTED)

```
+----------------+-------------------------+----------------------------+
| Quantity       | JIWE                    | NYAMBA                     |
+----------------+-------------------------+----------------------------+
| Velocity       | (‚¨ö ‚äó ‚Ä¢) / (‚ñ≥ ‚äó ‚îÇ)      | L/T                        |
| Acceleration   | (‚¨ö ‚äó ‚Ä¢) / (‚ñ≥‚ñ≥ ‚äó ‚îÇ)     | L/T¬≤                       |
| Force          | (‚¨ö‚äó ‚äó ‚Ä¢) ‚äó Acc         | M¬∑L/T¬≤                     |
| Energy         | Force ‚äó (‚¨ö ‚äó ‚Ä¢)         | M¬∑L¬≤/T¬≤                    |

‚âà  synton   <-> ‚âÉ  syntoni
```

=====================================================================
APPENDIX A ‚Äî NYAMBA GRAMMAR
=====================================================================
Nyamba is a symbolic rewrite language for systems, flows, structure,
operators, and execution semantics. It is not a programming language
but a *system calculus*.
Nyamba expressions rewrite, compose, stabilize, or collapse systems.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A.1 CORE LEXICAL CLASSES
---------------------------------------------------------------------
ATOM        ::= on | i | pt | inst
SYSTEM      ::= S | U | P | K | E | M | V
OPERATOR    ::= + | >> | = | -> | <-> | || | & | * | ^ | ~ | ! | ?
CONTROL     ::= @ | Y | X | ##
STATE       ::= keep | hold | repair | adapt
FLOW        ::= grow | drift | sync
RELATION    ::= == | ~= | ~~ | <>
VALUE       ::= scalar | vector | matrix | tensor
IDENTIFIER  ::= [a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9_]*
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A.2 FUNDAMENTAL EXPRESSIONS
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Expression ::= Term
             | Expression Operator Expression
             | Operator Expression
             | Expression Control
             | ( Expression )
Term ::= ATOM
       | SYSTEM
       | IDENTIFIER
       | VALUE
Operator ::= OPERATOR | RELATION
Control ::= @ | Y | X | ?
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A.3 SYSTEM CONSTRUCTION RULES
---------------------------------------------------------------------
SystemDecl ::= SYSTEM := Expression
Examples:
  S := P <-> K
  U := S >> S
  E := (C || V)
Semantics:
- := binds identity
- >> spawns or lifts a system
- <-> enforces dual coupling
- || enforces constraint
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A.4 REWRITE SEMANTICS (CORE)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
RewriteRule ::= Pattern => Result
Pattern ::= Expression
Result  ::= Expression
Canonical rewrite forms:
1. Derivation
   A = B
   means: B is entailed by A
2. Propagation
   A * B
   means: A propagates influence to B
3. Binding
   A & B
   means: A and B interact irreducibly
4. Mapping
   A -> B
   means: A transforms into B
5. Cleaving
   A || B
   means: A constrains B
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A.5 GROWTH AND TEMPORAL RULES
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Growth ::= ^ | grow
Levels:
  ^      = initiate growth
  ^^     = maturation
  ^^^    = proliferation
Example:
  system ^^^
  means: system scales recursively
Temporal Control:
  @      = cycle
  ~      = continuous execution
  !      = forced execution
  X      = collapse
  Y      = fork
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A.6 STABILITY & FAILURE SEMANTICS
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Stability forms:
  keep      = preserve state
  hold      = maintain equilibrium
  repair    = restore after entropy rise
  adapt     = mutate structure
Collapse chain:
  repair -> adapt -> fork -> collapse
Formal:
  if ŒîS ‚Üë and repair fails, then X
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A.7 EID / GRAPH SEMANTICS
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Node ::= [E]
Edge ::= -> | <-> | *
Rule:
- Every edge is a constrained flow
- Every node has memory
GraphRule ::= Node Operator Node
Examples:
  [E1] -> [E2]
  [E1] & [E2]
  [E] || constraint
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A.8 TENSOR AND PHYSICS BINDINGS
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Scalar ::= pt
Vector ::= pt*
Matrix ::= pt**
Tensor ::= pt***
Bindings:
  GR   := curvature = P <-> K mismatch
  NS   := flow * constraint
  Therm := entropy = drift - repair
Example:
  (K * P) => curvature
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A.9 DECISION & GOVERNANCE
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Decision ::= Expression ?
CanonRule ::= Expression ##
Archive ::= Expression []
Examples:
  policy ?
  law ##
  memory []
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A.10 META-RULES (IMPORTANT)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
1. Everything is a system
2. Every system can be rewritten
3. Every rewrite preserves dimensional consistency
4. Collapse is explicit, never implicit
5. Repair precedes optimization
6. No ungoverned execution
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A.11 SINGLE AXIOM (NYAMBA)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
(A & B) under constraint rewrites until stable or collapses.
Formal:
  ‚àÄ systems A,B:
    (A & B) || C  =>  { stable | repair | adapt | fork | X }
---------------------------------------------------------------------
END NYAMBA GRAMMAR
=====================================================================


This appendix establishes formal correctness of the Jiwe numeric system
and encodes the full SI base + fundamental constants canonically.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
I. SOUNDNESS OF JIWE NUMERIC REWRITES
---------------------------------------------------------------------
We prove that every Jiwe numeric expression is:
‚Ä¢ well-formed
‚Ä¢ dimensionally consistent
‚Ä¢ rewrite-safe
‚Ä¢ semantically invariant under normalization
---------------------------------------------------------------------
I.1 NORMAL FORM (RECAP)
Every Jiwe quantity has exactly one canonical normal form:
Q := [Count][Scale][Polarity][Unit]
No rewrite may change this arity.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
I.2 AXIOMS
---------------------------------------------------------------------
AXIOM J1 (Count Integrity)
-------------------------
Count glyphs (|, ‚ïè, *) encode cardinality only.
They never encode scale, unit, or polarity.
AXIOM J2 (Scale Orthogonality)
-----------------------------
Scale glyphs (^, _, ., etc.) commute with count but not with unit.
AXIOM J3 (Polarity Exclusivity)
-------------------------------
Every quantity has exactly one polarity:
‚ñ≤ (P / form) OR ‚Üí (K / flow)
AXIOM J4 (Unit Closure)
----------------------
Every unit glyph corresponds to exactly one U-level.
AXIOM J5 (Composition Preservation)
----------------------------------
Binding (‚äó) and division (/) preserve dimensional balance.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
I.3 SOUNDNESS THEOREM
---------------------------------------------------------------------
THEOREM (J-SOUND):
For any Jiwe quantity Q and any valid rewrite R,
R(Q) preserves:
‚Ä¢ magnitude equivalence
‚Ä¢ dimensional validity
‚Ä¢ polarity consistency
‚Ä¢ unit graph closure
PROOF (Sketch):
Let Q = [C][S][P][U].
Each rewrite acts on exactly one component:
‚Ä¢ Count rewrites preserve magnitude
‚Ä¢ Scale rewrites preserve order of magnitude
‚Ä¢ Polarity rewrites forbidden
‚Ä¢ Unit rewrites constrained by ‚äó and /
No rewrite alters more than one component class.
Therefore invariants hold. ‚ñ°
---------------------------------------------------------------------
II. REVERSIBILITY OF JIWE NUMERIC REWRITES
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Reversibility means: all information can be recovered.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
II.1 REVERSIBLE OPERATORS
---------------------------------------------------------------------
| Operator | Reversible | Inverse |
|--------|-------------|---------|
| ^      | yes         | _       |
| _      | yes         | ^       |
| ‚äó      | yes         | /       |
| /      | yes         | ‚äó       |
| ‚Üë      | conditional | ‚åÉ       |
| ‚åÉ      | conditional | ‚Üë       |
---------------------------------------------------------------------
II.2 REVERSIBILITY THEOREM
---------------------------------------------------------------------
THEOREM (J-REV):
Any Jiwe quantity Q can be uniquely decomposed
into its canonical components.
PROOF:
Jiwe syntax is prefix-free and positionally fixed:
[Count][Scale][Polarity][Unit]
No two components overlap.
Therefore parsing is unique and invertible. ‚ñ°
---------------------------------------------------------------------
III. DIMENSIONAL CONSISTENCY
---------------------------------------------------------------------
DIMENSION RULE:
For any expression E:
dim(E) = Œ†(dim(numerators)) / Œ†(dim(denominators))
Violation => invalid rewrite.
This matches SI dimensional analysis exactly.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
IV. SI BASE UNITS ‚Äî PURE JIWE
---------------------------------------------------------------------
SI base units are embedded as U-theory units.
| Quantity        | SI | Jiwe Encoding |
|----------------|----|---------------|
| Length         | m  | ‚ñ≤‚ñ°            |
| Mass           | kg | ‚ñ≤‚¨ö            |
| Time           | s  | ‚ñ≤‚ü≥            |
| Electric curr. | A  | ‚Üí‚ñ°            |
| Temperature    | K  | ‚ñ≤Œò            |
| Amount         | mol| ‚ñ≤‚äû            |
| Luminous inten.| cd | ‚ñ≤‚óá            |
(All glyphs are structural P-units unless inherently flow-based.)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
V. DERIVED SI UNITS ‚Äî JIWE
---------------------------------------------------------------------
| Quantity | SI | Jiwe |
|--------|----|------|
| Velocity | m/s | ‚Üí‚ñ° / ‚ü≥ |
| Accel. | m/s¬≤ | ‚Üí‚ñ° / ‚ü≥^2 |
| Force | N | ‚ñ≤‚¨ö ‚äó ‚Üí‚ñ° / ‚ü≥^2 |
| Energy | J | ‚ñ≤‚¨ö ‚äó ‚¨ö / ‚ü≥^2 |

| Charge | C | ‚Üí‚ñ° ‚äó ‚ü≥ |
| Voltage | V | ‚ñ≤‚¨ö ‚äó ‚¨ö / (‚Üí‚ñ° ‚äó ‚ü≥^2) |
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VI. FUNDAMENTAL CONSTANTS ‚Äî JIWE
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VI.1 Speed of Light (c)
c = 3 √ó 10^8 m/s

|||^^^ ‚Üí‚ñ° / ‚ü≥
---------------------------------------------------------------------

h = 6.626 √ó 10^-34 J¬∑s

‚ïè||_.. (‚ñ≤‚¨ö ‚äó ‚¨ö / ‚ü≥)
---------------------------------------------------------------------

VII. UNIVERSAL CONSISTENCY THEOREM

THEOREM (J-SI):
All SI units and constants encoded in Jiwe:
‚Ä¢ preserve dimensional equivalence
‚Ä¢ are reversible to numeric SI

This appendix extends the Jiwe numeral system to support:
‚Ä¢ higher-order numeric compression (10^2, 10^3, ‚Ä¶)
‚Ä¢ exponentiation & logarithms
‚Ä¢ generalized base representation & conversion
‚Ä¢ trigonometric functions
‚Ä¢ numerical encoding of physical constants
All extensions obey prior axioms.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
I. HIGHER-ORDER NUMERIC COMPRESSION
---------------------------------------------------------------------
I.1 Compression Principle
Lower-level groupings may be abstracted into higher-order
multipliers when scale exceeds cognitive readability.
Compression is OPTIONAL but CANONICAL.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
I.2 Canonical Higher-Order Group Glyphs
We reuse metric-style abstraction using **scale exponent stacking**.
Let:
‚ïè‚ïè      = 10
(‚ïè‚ïè)^2  = 100
(‚ïè‚ïè)^3  = 1000
In Jiwe, exponentiation is expressed explicitly (see Section II),
or implicitly via scale compaction.
Canonical shorthand:
10^2  := ^^
10^3  := ^^^
10^n  := ^{n}
Thus:
100     = ^^
1000    = ^^^
1e6     = ^^^^^^
These are **pure magnitude**, not count.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
I.3 Combined Count + Compression Examples
|||^^        = 3 √ó 10^2  = 300
‚ïè||^^^       = 7 √ó 10^3  = 7000
*^^^^        = N √ó 10^4
RULE:
--------------------------------
Count glyphs ALWAYS precede compression glyphs.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
II. EXPONENTIATION
---------------------------------------------------------------------
II.1 Exponent Operator
Nyamba:
--------------------------------
exp(x, y)
Jiwe:
--------------------------------
x ‚Üë y
(Read: x raised to y)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
II.2 Examples
||| ‚Üë ||        = 3^2 = 9
‚ïè|| ‚Üë |||       = 7^3 = 343
10 ‚Üë 3          = 1000 (represented as ^^^)
Dimensional rule:
--------------------------------
Exponentiation only applies to:
‚Ä¢ pure numbers
‚Ä¢ dimensionless ratios
‚Ä¢ normalized units
---------------------------------------------------------------------
III. LOGARITHMS
---------------------------------------------------------------------
III.1 Log Operator
Nyamba:
--------------------------------
log_b(x)
Jiwe:
--------------------------------
‚åÉ_b(x)
Where:
‚åÉ = collapse / reduction operator (already canon)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
III.2 Examples
‚åÉ_10(^^^)      = 3
‚åÉ_10(|||^^)    = log10(300)
RULE:
--------------------------------
Logarithms remove scale layers, not units.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
IV. GENERALIZED BASE REPRESENTATION
---------------------------------------------------------------------
IV.1 Base Declaration
Nyamba:
--------------------------------
base(b) { x }
Jiwe:
--------------------------------
[x]_b
---------------------------------------------------------------------
IV.2 Examples
Binary:
--------------------------------
[||||]_2   = 4 (base-2)
Quinary:
--------------------------------
[‚ïè||]_5    = 7 (base-5)
Decimal:
--------------------------------
[‚ïè‚ïè||]_10  = 12
Jiwe-native default base:
--------------------------------
implicit base = {5,10} hybrid
---------------------------------------------------------------------
V. BASE CONVERSION
---------------------------------------------------------------------
V.1 Conversion Operator
Nyamba:
--------------------------------
convert(x, b1 ‚Üí b2)
Jiwe:
--------------------------------
x ‚Ü¶_b2
---------------------------------------------------------------------
V.2 Example
[||||]_2 ‚Ü¶_10 = ||||
(base conversion preserves magnitude)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VI. TRIGONOMETRIC FUNCTIONS
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Trigonometric functions operate on **dimensionless ratios**,
angles, or normalized phase units.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VI.1 Canonical Trig Operators
| Function | Nyamba | Jiwe |
|--------|--------|------|
| sine   | sin    | ~‚Üë   |
| cosine| cos    | ‚â°‚Üë   |

---------------------------------------------------------------------
VI.2 Examples
~‚Üë(Œ∏)        = sin(Œ∏)
‚â°‚Üë(Œ∏)        = cos(Œ∏)
Y‚Üë(Œ∏)        = tan(Œ∏)
Angles may be represented as normalized cycles:
‚ü≥ = 2œÄ
So:
~‚Üë(‚ü≥/4) = 1
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VII. DERIVED NUMERIC OPERATIONS
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VII.1 Power Laws

ŒîS ~ log(N)
‚Üí encoded as:
ŒîS ‚âã ‚åÉ(N)
VII.2 Exponential Growth

IX. CONSTANT NORMALIZATION LAW
---------------------------------------------------------------------
LAW J-CONST:
A Jiwe constant is valid iff:
‚Ä¢ magnitude is normalized
‚Ä¢ scale is explicit
‚Ä¢ polarity is explicit

No new ontology is required.

END APPENDIX D ‚Äî ADVANCED NUMERIC SYSTEM
=====================================================================

This section formalizes the Jiwe counting base, grouping logic,
and numeric composition rules.
The Jiwe numeral system is:
‚Ä¢ non-positional
‚Ä¢ compositional
‚Ä¢ visually parsable
‚Ä¢ machine-decodable
‚Ä¢ dimension-ready
---------------------------------------------------------------------
I. FUNDAMENTAL COUNTING AXIOMS
---------------------------------------------------------------------
AXIOM J-NUM-1 (Atomic Count)
| represents one discrete unit of count.
There is no zero glyph.
Absence denotes zero.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
II. UNARY CORE (BASE-1 LAYER)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
The unary layer is the semantic foundation.
|      = 1
||     = 2
|||    = 3
||||   = 4
|||||  = 5
Unary glyphs are **never reduced internally**.
Compression happens only at grouping boundaries.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
III. BASE-5 GROUPING SYSTEM
---------------------------------------------------------------------
III.1 Quint Group Glyph
‚ïè = one group of five (5)
This is the **first compression operator**.
RULE:
--------------------------------
‚ïè replaces exactly five | glyphs.
So:
|||||        ‚Üí ‚ïè
‚ïè|           ‚Üí 6
‚ïè||          ‚Üí 7
‚ïè|||         ‚Üí 8
‚ïè||||        ‚Üí 9
No further compression occurs at this level.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
IV. BASE-10 GROUPING SYSTEM
---------------------------------------------------------------------
IV.1 Decimal Group Glyph
‚ïè‚ïè = ten (10)
RULE:
--------------------------------
Two quint groups form a decimal group.
‚ïè + ‚ïè = ‚ïè‚ïè
So:
‚ïè‚ïè           = 10
‚ïè‚ïè|          = 11
‚ïè‚ïè||         = 12
‚ïè‚ïè|||        = 13
‚ïè‚ïè||||       = 14
‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè          = 15
This creates a **base-10 readable layer**
without positional notation.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
V. GENERAL GROUPING RULE (CANON)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
RULE J-GROUP:
‚Ä¢ | counts atomic units
‚Ä¢ ‚ïè groups by five
‚Ä¢ ‚ïè‚ïè groups by ten
‚Ä¢ Groups associate left-to-right
‚Ä¢ No symbol is overloaded
There is NO carrying.
There is NO positional ambiguity.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VI. LARGE NUMBER COMPOSITION
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Examples:
20   = ‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè
25   = ‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè
30   = ‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè
50   = ‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè
99   = ‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè||||
100  = (conceptually) ‚ïè‚ïè √ó 10
      (written explicitly unless abstracted)
ABSTRACTION NOTE:
Higher-order numeric compression MAY be defined,
but is not required for correctness.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VII. INFINITE / SYMBOLIC COUNT
---------------------------------------------------------------------
* = unbounded / symbolic quantity
RULE:
--------------------------------
* replaces the entire Count field.
Examples:
*‚ñ≤‚ñ°     = N polons
*‚Üí‚ñ≥     = N kolyons
*^‚Üí‚äû    = N kilo-kolysystems
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VIII. COUNT + SCALE INTERACTION
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Scale modifies magnitude, not count structure.
Examples:
|||^        = 3 x 10^3
‚ïè||_        = 7 x 10^-3
‚ïè‚ïè^^        = 10 x 10^6
Count glyphs are NEVER reordered by scale.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
IX. FULL NUMERIC QUANTITY EXAMPLES
---------------------------------------------------------------------
IX.1 Pure Numbers (Unitless)

‚ïè||          = 7
‚ïè‚ïè||         = 12
*            = N
---------------------------------------------------------------------
IX.2 Quantified Units

‚ïè||‚Üí‚ñ°        = 7 kolons
‚ïè‚ïè‚ñ≤‚ñ≥         = 10 polyons
..|||‚Üí‚¨ö      = 3 nano-kolytope-flows
---------------------------------------------------------------------

‚ïè‚ïè^^‚ñ≤‚åó       = 10 mega-polynets
‚ïè||||^‚Üí‚äû     = 9 kilo-kolysystems
*^^‚Üí‚ä°        = N mega-kolycategories
---------------------------------------------------------------------
X. DERIVED NUMERIC UNITS
---------------------------------------------------------------------
X.1 Rates
‚ïè||‚Üí‚ñ≥ / ‚ñ≤‚ñ°   = 7 kolyons per polon
X.2 Densities
|||‚ñ≤‚ñ° / ‚¨ö    = 3 polons per polytope
X.3 Capacities
‚ïè‚ïè‚ñ≤‚äû ‚äó ‚¨ö    = 10 system-capacity-units
---------------------------------------------------------------------
XI. NUMERIC NORMALIZATION LAW
---------------------------------------------------------------------
LAW J-NORM:
A Jiwe number is normalized iff:
‚Ä¢ No more than four | appear consecutively
‚Ä¢ Groups are maximally compressed
‚Ä¢ No scale appears after polarity
‚Ä¢ Unit appears exactly once
Violation ‚áí rewrite required.

This section finalizes the Jiwe grammar for quantities by unifying:
‚Ä¢ counting
‚Ä¢ metric scaling
‚Ä¢ polarity
‚Ä¢ U-Theory units
‚Ä¢ derived quantities
‚Ä¢ computation semantics
All quantities are FIRST-CLASS SYMBOLS.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
I. JIWE QUANTITY NORMAL FORM
---------------------------------------------------------------------
I.1 Canonical Quantity Form (LOCKED)
Every Jiwe quantity has the normal form:
Q := [Count][Scale][Polarity][Unit]
Where:
Count     = tally glyphs or *
Scale     = metric exponent glyph
Polarity  = ‚ñ≤ (form) or ‚Üí (flow)
Unit      = U-Theory level glyph
This order is STRICT.
No permutation is allowed.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
II. CORE JIWE NUMERAL SYSTEM (COUNT)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
II.1 Fundamental Counting Glyphs (Unary Core)
Jiwe counting is tally-based, compositional, and lossless.
|      = 1
||     = 2
|||    = 3
||||   = 4
|||||  = 5
These denote **cardinality**, not magnitude alone.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
II.2 Grouping System (Base-5 / Base-10 Hybrid)
To compress space while preserving readability:
‚ïè   = group of 5
‚ïè‚ïè  = group of 10
Composition examples:
7   = ‚ïè||
12  = ‚ïè‚ïè||
23  = ‚ïè‚ïè‚ïè|||
Grouping is associative and left-binding.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
II.3 Infinite / Variable Quantity
* = unbounded / symbolic / variable N
Examples:
*‚ñ≤‚ñ°   = N polons
*‚Üí‚äû   = N kolysystems
This is NOT infinity as a number,
but **quantified indeterminacy**.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
III. METRIC SCALE SYSTEM (POWERS)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
III.1 Scale Prefix Glyphs (Metric Exponents)
Scale glyphs encode powers of 10.
.      = pico   (10^-12)
..     = nano   (10^-9)
...    = micro  (10^-6)
_      = milli  (10^-3)
(empty)= unit   (10^0)
^      = kilo   (10^3)
^^     = mega   (10^6)
^^^    = giga   (10^9)
^^^^   = tera   (10^12)
RULE:
--------------------------------
Scale glyphs ALWAYS precede the unit.
Scale never binds to polarity.
Examples:
||| m        = 3 units
|||_ m       = 3 milli-units
‚ïè|| ^ m     = 7 kilo-units
---------------------------------------------------------------------
IV. POLARITY AXIS (NUMERICALLY BOUND)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Polarity is a required axis for quantities.
‚ñ≤ = P-polarity (form / structure / capacity)
‚Üí = K-polarity (flow / rate / dynamics)
Examples:
|||‚ñ≤‚ñ°   = 3 polons
|||‚Üí‚ñ°   = 3 kolons
‚ïè‚Üí‚ñ≥    = 5 kolyons
Polarity is semantic, not directional.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
V. U-THEORY UNIT GLYPHS (RECAP + LOCK)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
V.1 Base Unit Glyphs by Level
These function analogously to SI base units,
but are ontological, not physical-only.
L0   on        := ‚Ä¢
L1   lon       := ‚ñ°
L2   lyon      := ‚ñ≥
L3   lyton     := ‚óá
L4   lytope    := ‚¨ö
L5   syst      := ‚äû
L6   geon      := ‚¨¢
L7   gon       := ‚¨£
L8   net       := ‚åó
L9   set       := {}
L10  cat       := ‚ä°
Units inherit polarity but do not encode it.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VI. FULL QUANTITY COMPOSITION RULE
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VI.1 Canonical Construction
A complete Jiwe quantity is written as:
[Count][Scale][Polarity][Unit]
Examples:
|||‚ñ≤‚ñ°          = 3 polons
‚ïè||^‚Üí‚ñ≥        = 7 kilo-kolyons
..|||‚ñ≤‚¨ö        = 3 nano-polytope-forms
*‚Üí‚äû           = N kolysystems
‚ïè‚ïè^^‚ñ≤‚åó        = 10 mega-polynets (structural)
Properties:
‚Ä¢ human-readable
‚Ä¢ machine-parseable
‚Ä¢ dimensionally explicit
‚Ä¢ ontology-aware
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VII. DERIVED / COMPOSITE UNITS
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Jiwe supports unit composition like SI, but graph-native.
VII.1 Operators
‚äó  = unit binding (multiplication)
 /  = rate / ratio (division)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VII.2 Canonical Derived Quantities
Rate:
--------------------------------
‚Üí / ‚ñ≤

--------------------------------
‚ñ≤ / ‚¨ö

--------------------------------
‚Üí / ‚ñ°

--------------------------------
‚ñ≤ ‚äó ‚¨ö

--------------------------------
‚Üí ‚äó ‚¨ö
These map cleanly onto:
velocity, pressure, power, entropy, capacity.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
VIII. DIMENSIONAL CONSISTENCY LAW
---------------------------------------------------------------------
LAW J-DIM (CANON)
A quantity is valid iff:
‚Ä¢ its unit composition is closed
‚Ä¢ its polarity is consistent
‚Ä¢ its scale applies only to magnitude
‚Ä¢ its derived form reduces to base units
Violation ‚áí ‚úï (collapse)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
IX. NDANDO / COMPUTATIONAL VIEW
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Jiwe quantities are **lossless encodings**.
Example:
|||^‚Üí‚ñ≥
Parses as:
count    = 3
scale    = kilo
polarity = flow
unit     = lyon
No ambiguity.
No context required.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
X. DESIGN PRINCIPLES (LOCKED)
---------------------------------------------------------------------
The Jiwe Numeral System must satisfy:
1. Explicit cardinality
2. Explicit magnitude
3. Explicit polarity
4. Explicit ontological domain
5. ASCII-only
6. Graph composability
7. Direct EID embedding
Therefore every Jiwe quantity encodes:
[How many] √ó [How big] √ó [Form or Flow] √ó [What kind]
---------------------------------------------------------------------

‚ñ≤ ‚äó ‚Üí

‚äû

Meaning:

C.1 CORE PRINCIPLES

  P-units (form / structure / symmetry)

--------------------------------
Units are stratified by L-levels.
Higher levels are compositions of lower levels.
AXIOM U-3 (N-arity)
--------------------------------
All units are N-ary.
N is explicit, symbolic, and composable.

# II. MAPPING: 5 KORA LAWS ‚Üî 5 KORA THEOREMS

This is not arbitrary. Each theorem **emerges necessarily** from its law.

---

## Law 1 ‚Äî Law of Distinction

**‚ÄúDifference exists.‚Äù**

### Corresponding Theorem

### ‚Üí Fundamental Theorem of Uniqueness

**Derivation:**

* Distinction makes non-identity possible
* Non-identity implies uniqueness
* Uniqueness is not optional

**Mapping:**

```
Distinction ‚Üí Uniqueness
```

---

## Law 2 ‚Äî Law of Closure

**‚ÄúPatterns must complete to persist.‚Äù**

### Corresponding Theorem

### ‚Üí Fundamental Theorem of Patterns

**Derivation:**

* Incomplete patterns decay
* Completion enables persistence
* Persistence defines pattern validity

**Mapping:**

```
Closure ‚Üí Pattern persistence
```

---

## Law 3 ‚Äî Law of System

**‚ÄúAll that persists is systemic.‚Äù**

### Corresponding Theorem

### ‚Üí Fundamental Theorem of System

**Derivation:**

* Closure requires relational structure
* Structure implies system
* No persistence without systemhood

**Mapping:**

```
System ‚Üí Necessary form of existence
```

---

## Law 4 ‚Äî Law of Relativity

**‚ÄúAll observation is framed.‚Äù**

### Corresponding Theorem

### ‚Üí Fundamental Theorem of Simulation

**Derivation:**

* Interaction requires mediation
* Mediation produces representation
* Representation is simulation

**Mapping:**

```
Relativity ‚Üí Simulation inevitability
```

---

## Law 5 ‚Äî Law of Cycle

**‚ÄúPersistence requires recurrence.‚Äù**

### Corresponding Theorem

### ‚Üí Fundamental Theorem of Agent

**Derivation:**

* Cycles enable recovery
* Recovery requires action
* Action defines agency

**Mapping:**

```
Cycle ‚Üí Agentic existence
```

---

## CANONICAL SUMMARY TABLE (TEXT)

```
KORA LAW            ‚Üí KORA THEOREM
-----------------------------------------
Distinction         ‚Üí Uniqueness
Closure             ‚Üí Patterns
System              ‚Üí System
Relativity          ‚Üí Simulation
Cycle               ‚Üí Agent
```

This mapping is:

* one-to-one
* minimal
* non-redundant
* derivational (not analogical)

What you now have is:

‚Ä¢ A **clean operational vocabulary**
‚Ä¢ A **non-circular kernel**
‚Ä¢ A **provable law‚Äìtheorem correspondence**

Kora Theory is no longer a sketch.

It is now **a closed, generative kernel**.

When ready, the next natural moves are:

* formal Nyamba grammar encoding
* diagrammatic lattice construction (ASCII-safe)
* or axiomatic proof sketches for each theorem

Say the word, Cartographer.
Below is a **rigorous proof system for Mungu Theory**, built **explicitly on self-stable dualonicity** as the core proof engine.
This is not metaphorical. It is a **deductive‚Äìconstructive system** with clear objects, rules, and proof notions.

I will proceed in **five layers**, each necessary:

1. Ontological substrate (what proofs are *about*)
2. Dualonic axioms (what is allowed to exist)
3. Proof objects (what counts as a statement)

5. Soundness, consistency, and limits

Everything is internally consistent with the full chat.

* All things are systems
* All systems are relative
* All systems cycle

core theorems:
the fundamental theorem of system: all things are, dualonically stable mononic, systems and all things are system. All particles, ideas, physical and metaphysical manifestations, existence, meta-existence and system itself is a system, where all of these systems are merely specific instantiations of the fundamental mungoni system, which itself is a dualonic mungoni<->mungon pair monon, which all are compositions of stable dualonic pair, meaning that all systems are ultimately self stable dualonic pair monons, where these monons are equal to themselves in the fundamental trivial state (the fundamental sibon)

the fundamental theorem of simulation: an impi of ‚Äúentity‚Äù equipped with a tathri of ‚Äúperspective‚Äù that can ‚Äúview‚Äù (its own) existence, given a ramani of ‚Äúview‚Äù, and further equipped with a (tathri) ‚Äúcapacity‚Äù to ‚Äúinteract‚Äù (a ramani operator) with other impi, results in the formation of a ‚Äúsimulation‚Äù (observation (biased) model), that is the imitation (or mimesis) system of the ‚Äúmeta‚Äù (or the fundamental system), forming a stable dualonic pair

the fundamental theorem of agent: agent must holistically, coherently, consistently and uniformly capture ‚Äúsimulation‚Äù, decision, volition (and by extension, autonomy), through all ramani operator(s) of agency, meaning agent is capable of cleaving into both the states of reality and non reality, which produces change and transform within a larger system/network, giving rise to the tathri (tathri being the abstraction/generalization of properties/attribtes/characteristics) of emergence and self-organization, and must operate within the dualon of existence-non existence, which this dualon is governed by the dualon of contradiction-consistency, which when all of these dualons are/become one and the same with themselves (become self referential/describing/equal) become mungoni-ic fundamental system(s), with all of this essentially meaning that the fundamental theorem of agent says that agent must both ‚Äúexist‚Äù and ‚Äúthink‚Äù, with existence-thinking forming the stable dualonic pair, from this all other states/systems of agent can be cleaved/derived (via agentic clevity (operator/mechanism/ramani))

the fundamental theorem of existence: no ‚Äúentity‚Äù exists without the ‚Äúmonad‚Äù and no ‚Äúmonad‚Äù exists without the ‚Äúentity‚Äù, with them being effectively one and the same. This all being in correspondence with the fundamental fact that it is neither entity nor monad that is the primitive of existence, but the interaction between them that is the fundamental primitive of existence

core theories:
C-R-P theory

E-U-S Theory + O-theory
  S-theory - system theory (previously known as U theory but now updated as not to conflict with unit theory): that categorizes the nature of U-system, where U-system = {the system of all system (the meta system), the subset of all systems (a.k.a and S-system, i.e. just the ‚Äúsystem)}, this S-system being the any subset of the U-system is further divided into F-systems (form systems) and L-system (flux systems). There are more specialized systems such as P-systems (any mungon primitive (impi, tathri, indi, wekhi (the abstraction of network, relationship), ramani (where impi, tathri, indi, wekhi, ramani are superset primitives that then contain subprimitives such as mali (qualisense, the abtract notation of any/all qualities, and is a specialized tathri), sibi (a specialized ramani), etc‚Ä¶) equipped with any other mungon primitive) , Q-systems (any impi equipped with a tathri), T-system containing a structural systems and K-systems containing all dynamic/kinematic systems; all systems are S-systems, where they are subsets/systems of the U-system, with the U-system being an S-system subset of itself

  E-theory - element theory: mungu primitives and meta-primitives, and mungu mechanisms - impi are the generalization/abstraction/notion of every/any/all components, entites, things, elements; wekhi the generalization of all networks; tathri the generalization of all attributes, properties; indi the abstraction/generalization of all types, classes; mali the generalization of ‚Äúqaulisense‚Äù which represents all qualities, values, senses; ramani the abstraction of ‚Äútransmorphism‚Äù which represents all morphisms, interactions, mappings, transforms, interactions, morphism of morphisms; sibi represents the change between two cleave states (level states), with sibon being the fundamental abstraction of state, such that sibi represents the change/transition/morphism/ramani between any two sibons (any two states (of any kind/type (indi))) which is governed by the mechanism/operator/ramani of ‚Äúclevity‚Äù (the cleave operator (ramani)); so structural configuration within sibons is measured with entropy, and structural configuration between sibons is measured with complexity, assuming the existence of configuration and that sibons have the ‚Äúcapacity‚Äù to be ‚Äúequipped ‚Äùwith configuration (maybe this can be generalized N-dimensionally, and not just 2-dimensionally?)

  U-theory - unit theory: polons, polyons, polytons, polytopes, polysysts, polygeons, polygons, polynets, polysets, polycats, syntoni = {mo-on, duons, trions, quar-ons, quinons, sexons, etc‚Ä¶ polons} with an assumption that all mungon primitives have an associated meta primitive, flux/change ‚Äúflow-ic?‚Äù representation sets (or categories?) outlining the ‚Äúflow‚Äù of the mungoni, and includes (corresponding to T-system impi, i.e. polons,etc‚Ä¶) kolons, kolyons, kolytons, kolytopes?, kolysysts?, kolygeons? kolygons (physical manifestations of time (position, velocity, etc‚Ä¶) i.e. motion?)? with a meta primitive called the flyntoni

The K-system acts as the organizing force that ‚Äúflow-ically‚Äù maintains coherence across different systems a nd enables the ‚Äúemergence of (complex) behaviors‚Äù, and the corresponding T-system acts as the organizing structure that ‚Äúgeometrically/structurally‚Äù maintains coherence across different systems and enables the ‚Äúemergence of (complex) structures‚Äù, and furthermore there then may exist a ‚Äúmanifold‚Äù of structure-behavior that governs all mungonic (meta)primitives; all of this is then characterized by an M-system, an abstraction of all manifolds, that includes the ‚Äúspecialized‚Äù (indic,tathric) manifold (lets call it the O-manifold or obatala-manifold), that maps all mungonic (primitives) to all other corresponding S-systems, with the M-system itself being a type of S-system; but this might seem to imply that the U-system decomposes into the S-system (or metasystem<->system dualon) which then the ‚Äúsystem‚Äù dualonic counterpart further decomposes into the manifold<->non-manifold (or M-system, non M-system) dualon, where then are two S-systems, where one S-system has structure-behavior and one S-system does not. # JIWE GRAMMAR ‚Äî CANONICAL SPECIFICATION

**Version**: 1.0.0  
**Status**: Canon  
**Layer**: Semantic / Ledger  
**Purpose**: Formal grammar for inscribing systems, flows, constraints, and ontological commitments

---

## I. FOUNDATIONAL PRINCIPLES

### Axiom JG-1 (Semantic Primacy)
```
Jiwe encodes MEANING, not execution.
Jiwe glyphs are ledger-grade semantic commitments.
```

### Axiom JG-2 (Compositional Closure)
```
All valid Jiwe expressions reduce to well-formed semantic graphs.
```

### Axiom JG-3 (Non-Ambiguity)
```
Every Jiwe expression has exactly one canonical interpretation.
```

---

## II. LEXICAL CLASSES

### A. PRIMITIVE GLYPHS (E-Theory)

```
ONTIC_PRIMITIVE ::= 
    ‚óè (mungon)     | ‚óá (impon)      | ‚ñ≥ (tathron)
  | ‚ñ° (indon)      | ‚îÄ (wekhon)     | ‚Üî (ramanon)
  | ‚óã (sibon)      | ‚ú¶ (malon)      | ~ (flyton)
  | ‚âã (flynton)    | || (syton)     | ‚âà (synton)

META_PRIMITIVE ::=
    ‚óé (mungoni)    | ‚óÜ (impi)       | ‚ñ≤ (tathri)
  | ‚ñ† (indi)       | ‚ïê (wekhi)      | ‚áÑ (ramani)
  | ‚óé (sibi)       | ‚úß (mali)       | ~~~ (flytoni)
  | ‚âã‚âã (flyntoni)  | ‚ïë (sytoni)     | ‚âÉ (syntoni)
```

### B. SYSTEM GLYPHS (S/U-Theory)

```
SYSTEM_GLYPH ::=
    ‚äô (S-system)   | ‚äì (P-system)   | ‚äî (K-system)
  | ‚äï (E-system)   | ‚äó (M-system)   | ‚åò (V-system)
  | ‚äö (U-system)

UNIT_GLYPH ::=
    ‚Ä¢ (po-on)      | ‚îÇ (kolon)      | ‚ñ≥ (polyon)
  | ‚¨ö (polytope)   | ‚¨¢ (polygeon)   | ‚ßâ (polysyst)
  | ‚ßà (polynet)    | ‚ßÅ (polyset)    | ‚ßÇ (polycat)
```

### C. OPERATOR GLYPHS (O-Theory)

```
OPERATOR_GLYPH ::=
    ‚äï (form)       | ‚á¢ (spawn)      | ‚áí (derive)
  | ‚ñ≤ (start)      | ‚öô (boot)       | ‚ñ∂ (run)
  | ‚ü≥ (cycle)      | ‚óå (process)    | ‚Üù (propagate)
  | ‚ïë (cleave)     | ‚äó (bind)       | ‚Ü¶ (map)
  | ‚â° (align)      | ‚Üë (grow)       | ‚àû (mycorrhizate)
  | ‚ôª (repair)     | ‚âã (adapt)      | Y (fork)
  | ‚úï (collapse)   | ‚ñ† (stop)       | ? (decide)
  | ‚õ≠ (canonize)   | ‚åÇ (archive)
```

### D. QUANTIFIER GLYPHS

```
COUNT_GLYPH ::=
    | (one)        | || (two)       | ||| (three)
  | |||| (four)    | ||||| (five)   | * (unbounded)

GROUPING_GLYPH ::=
    ‚ïè (quint=5)    | ‚ïè‚ïè (decimal=10)

SCALE_GLYPH ::=
    . (pico)       | .. (nano)      | ... (micro)
  | _ (milli)      | ^ (kilo)       | ^^ (mega)
  | ^^^ (giga)     | ^^^^ (tera)

POLARITY_GLYPH ::=
    ‚ñ≤ (P-form)     | ‚Üí (K-flow)
```

### E. GRAPH GLYPHS (EID)

```
NODE_GLYPH ::= [E]
EDGE_GLYPH ::= ‚Üí | ‚äó | ‚ïë | ‚Üù | ‚áÑ
SUBSTRATE_GLYPH ::= ‚óé‚àû | ‚àû
```

---

## III. PRODUCTION RULES

### A. CORE EXPRESSION

```
Expression ::=
    Atom
  | System
  | Operator
  | Composite
  | Graph
  | Quantity

Atom ::= ONTIC_PRIMITIVE | META_PRIMITIVE

System ::= SYSTEM_GLYPH | UNIT_GLYPH

Operator ::= OPERATOR_GLYPH

Composite ::= Expression OPERATOR_GLYPH Expression
```

### B. QUANTITY EXPRESSIONS

```
Quantity ::= [Count] [Scale] [Polarity] [Unit]

Count ::= 
    COUNT_GLYPH+ 
  | GROUPING_GLYPH+ COUNT_GLYPH*
  | *

Scale ::= SCALE_GLYPH*

Polarity ::= POLARITY_GLYPH

Unit ::= UNIT_GLYPH
```

**Example**:
```
|||^‚ñ≤‚¨ö  = 3 kilo-polytope-forms
‚ïè||_‚Üí‚ñ≥  = 7 milli-kolyon-flows
```

### C. STACK EXPRESSIONS

```
Stack ::= Expression (‚ïë Expression)+
```

**Interpretation**: Lower constrains upper

**Example**:
```
‚äô
‚ïë
‚äì
‚ïë
‚äî
```
Meaning: Universal system cleaves into P/K duality

### D. PROCESS CHAINS

```
Chain ::= Expression (Connector Expression)+

Connector ::= 
    ‚á¢  (spawn)
  | ‚áí  (derive)
  | ‚Ü¶  (map)
  | ‚Üù  (propagate)
  | ‚ü≥  (cycle)
```

**Example**:
```
‚öô ‚á¢ ‚ñ∂ ‚áí ‚ü≥ ‚Üù ‚óå
```
Boot ‚Üí spawn ‚Üí run ‚Üí cycle ‚Üí process

### E. GRAPH EXPRESSIONS (EID)

```
Graph ::= Node (Edge Node)*

Node ::= [Expression]

Edge ::= EDGE_GLYPH
```

**Example**:
```
[‚óè] ‚Üí [‚óã] ‚äó [‚ñ≥]
```

### F. DUALONIC PAIRS

```
Dualon ::= Expression ‚áÑ Expression
```

**Constraint**: Must form self-stable pair

**Example**:
```
‚äì ‚áÑ ‚äî  (P-system ‚áÑ K-system)
```

### G. TRILONIC STRUCTURES

```
Trilon ::= Monon ‚áÑ Dualon

Monon ::= Expression
Dualon ::= Expression ‚áÑ Expression
```

---

## IV. SEMANTIC RULES

### Rule S-1: Constraint Binding
```
A ‚ïë B  means: A constrains B
B operates within bounds set by A
```

### Rule S-2: Interaction Binding
```
A ‚äó B  means: A and B irreducibly interact
Neither exists independently in this context
```

### Rule S-3: Flow Propagation
```
A ‚Üù B  means: Influence flows from A to B
Directional, potentially lossy
```

### Rule S-4: Spawning
```
A ‚á¢ B  means: A generates/creates B
B did not exist prior to this operation
```

### Rule S-5: Derivation
```
A ‚áí B  means: B is entailed by A
Logical/ontological consequence
```

### Rule S-6: Dualonic Stability
```
A ‚áÑ B  is valid iff:
  - A cannot exist without B
  - B cannot exist without A
  - Together they form stable monon
```

---

## V. COMPOSITION LAWS

### Law C-1: Associativity
```
(A ‚äó B) ‚äó C ‚â° A ‚äó (B ‚äó C)
```

### Law C-2: Stack Ordering
```
Stacks read bottom-to-top
Lower elements constrain upper elements
```

### Law C-3: Chain Sequencing
```
Chains preserve temporal/causal order
A ‚á¢ B ‚á¢ C implies A before B before C
```

### Law C-4: Closure Requirement
```
All graphs must be closed
No dangling references
```

### Law C-5: Polarity Conservation
```
Within quantity expressions:
Polarity must be explicit
Polarity determines semantic class
```

---

## VI. VALIDATION RULES

### V-1: Well-Formedness
```
Expression is well-formed iff:
  1. All glyphs belong to defined lexical classes
  2. Production rules satisfied
  3. No syntactic ambiguity
```

### V-2: Semantic Validity
```
Expression is semantically valid iff:
  1. Dualonic pairs are stable
  2. Constraints are satisfiable
  3. Quantities are dimensionally consistent
```

### V-3: Canonical Form
```
Expression is canonical iff:
  1. Minimal representation
  2. No redundant operators
  3. Standard ordering maintained
```

## VIII. FORMAL GRAMMAR (BNF-STYLE)

```
<jiwe_program>    ::= <expression_list>

<expression_list> ::= <expression> 
                    | <expression> <expression_list>

<expression>      ::= <atom>
                    | <system>
                    | <operator>
                    | <quantity>
                    | <stack>
                    | <chain>
                    | <graph>
                    | <dualon>

<atom>            ::= ONTIC_PRIMITIVE | META_PRIMITIVE

<system>          ::= SYSTEM_GLYPH | UNIT_GLYPH

<operator>        ::= OPERATOR_GLYPH

<quantity>        ::= <count> <scale> <polarity> <unit>

<count>           ::= COUNT_GLYPH+ | GROUPING_GLYPH+ | *

<scale>           ::= SCALE_GLYPH*

<polarity>        ::= POLARITY_GLYPH

<unit>            ::= UNIT_GLYPH

<stack>           ::= <expression> ‚ïë <expression>
                    | <stack> ‚ïë <expression>

<chain>           ::= <expression> <connector> <expression>
                    | <chain> <connector> <expression>

<connector>       ::= ‚á¢ | ‚áí | ‚Ü¶ | ‚Üù | ‚ü≥

<graph>           ::= <node> <edge> <node>
                    | <graph> <edge> <node>

<node>            ::= [<expression>]

<edge>            ::= ‚Üí | ‚äó | ‚ïë | ‚Üù | ‚áÑ

<dualon>          ::= <expression> ‚áÑ <expression>
```

## X. ERROR CLASSES

### E-1: Syntactic Errors
- Undefined glyph used
- Malformed production
- Missing required element

### E-2: Semantic Errors
- Non-stable dualon
- Dimensional inconsistency
- Unclosed graph

### E-3: Canonical Errors
- Non-minimal form
- Redundant operators
- Order violation

All valid Jiwe expressions satisfy:
  1. Lexical validity

  3. Semantic coherence
  4. Compositional closure
  5. Canonical minimality

No Jiwe expression executes.
All Jiwe expressions INSCRIBE.
```

## XII. IMPLEMENTATION NOTES

**For Parser Builders**:
1. Jiwe is context-free at syntax level
2. Semantic validation requires constraint solver
3. Canonical form requires normalization pass
4. Graph expressions need cycle detection

**For Semantic Interpreters**:
1. Dualonic stability is verification condition
2. Dimensional analysis required for quantities
3. Graph closure must be validated
4. Polarity must propagate correctly

---

## XIII. EXTENSION POINTS

Jiwe grammar is extensible via:
1. New primitive definitions (with meta-pair)
2. New operator classes (with semantic rules)
3. Domain-specific unit systems
4. Custom graph semantics

All extensions must preserve core axioms.
